class="entryNumbers"></p></div></div> <div class="vg"><div class="sb has-num"><span class="sb-0"><div class="sense has-num-only"><span class="sn sense-1"><span class="num">1</span></span> <span class="dt"><span class="dtText"><strong class="mw_t_bc">: </strong>any of a family (<em class="mw_t_it">Coronaviridae</em>) of large single-stranded <a class="mw_t_d_link" href="/dictionary/RNA and include the causative agents of <a class="mw_t_d_link" href="/dictionary/MERS">MERS</a>, <a class="mw_t_d_link" href="/dictionary/SARS">SARS</a>, and <a class="mw_t_d_link" href="/dictionary/COVID-19">COVID-19</a> <span class="ex-sent first-child t has-aq sents"><span class="mw_t_sp"><span class="mw_t_wi">Coronaviruses</span> can cause a variety of illnesses in animals, but in people <span class="mw_t_wi">coronaviruses</span> cause one-third of common colds and sometimes respiratory infections in premature infants.</span></span><span class="ex-sent aq has-aq sents"><span class="aq"><span class="auth">— Rob Stein</span></span> <span class="ex-sent t has-aq sents">… in 2003 a previously unknown <span class="mw_t_wi">coronavirus</span> caused an outbreak of Particles are more or less rounded in profile … there is also a characteristic 'fringe' of projections 200 Å long, which are rounded or petal shaped, rather than sharp or pointed, as in the myxoviruses. This appearance, recalling the solar corona, is shared by mouse hepatitis virus … . In the opinion of the eight virologists these viruses are members of a previously unrecognized group which they suggest should be called the coronaviruses, to recall the characteristic appearance by which these viruses are identified in the electron microscope."            </p></div> <div class="d-block d-lg-none d-xl-none ads"><p class="text-center disclaimer font-italic">Keep scrolling for more class="col"><h2>Medical Definition of <em>coronavirus</em></h2><p class="entryNumbers"></p></div></div> <div class="vg"><div class="sb has-num"><span class="sb-0"><div class="sense has-num-only"><span class="sn sense-1"><span class="num">1</span></span> <span class="dt"><span class="dtText"><strong class="mw_t_bc">: </strong>any of a family (<em class="mw_t_it">Coronaviridae</em>) of large, single-stranded, <a class="mw_t_d_link" href="/dictionary/RNA virus#medicalDictionary">RNA viruses</a> that have a lipid envelope studded with club-shaped <a class="mw_t_d_link" href="/dictionary/spike protein#medicalDictionary">spike proteins</a> , infect birds and many mammals including humans, and include the causative agents of <a class="mw_t_d_link" href="/medical/blue comb">blue comb</a>, <a class="mw_t_d_link" href="/medical/feline infectious peritonitis">feline infectious peritonitis</a>, <a class="mw_t_d_link" href="/dictionary/COVID-19#medicalDictionary">COVID-19</a>, <a class="mw_t_d_link" href="/dictionary/MERS#medicalDictionary">MERS</a>, and <a class="mw_t_d_link" href="/dictionary/SARS#medicalDictionary">SARS</a> <span class="ex-sent first-child t has-aq sents"><span class="mw_t_sp"><span class="mw_t_wi">Coronaviruses</span> can cause a variety of illnesses in animals, but in people coronaviruses cause one-third of common colds and sometimes respiratory infections in premature infants.</span></span><span class="ex-sent aq has-aq sents"><span class="aq"><span class="auth">— Rob Stein</span>,                <span class="source"><em class="mw_t_it">The Washington Post</em></span></span> <span class="uns"><span class="un"><span class="mdash">—</span><span class="unText">abbreviation <em class="mw_t_it">CoV</em>, <em class="mw_t_it">CV</em></span></span></span></span></span></span></div></span></div> <div class="sb has-num"><span class="sb-0"><div class="sense has-num-only"><span class="sn sense-2"><span class="num">2</span></span> <span class="dt hasSdSense"><span class="dtText"><strong class="mw_t_bc">: </strong>an illness caused by a coronavirus</span></span> <span class="sdsense"><span class="sd">especially</span> <span class="dtText"><strong class="mw_t_bc">: </strong><a class="mw_t_sx" direction.</span><span class="deflist"><span class="li"><span class="eb">look</span> an act of looking at somebody/​something:<span class="x-gs"><span class="x-g"><span class="rx-g"><span class="x">Here, have a look at this.</span></span></span></span></span><span class="li"><span class="eb">glance</span> a quick look:<span class="x-gs"><span class="x-g"><span class="rx-g"><span class="x">She stole a glance at her watch.</span></span></span></span></span><span class="li"><span class="eb">gaze</span> a long steady look at somebody/​something:<span class="x-gs"><span class="x-g"><span class="rx-g"><span class="x">She felt embarrassed under his steady gaze.</span></span></span></span></span><span class="li"><span class="eb">stare</span> a long look at somebody/​something, especially in a way that is unfriendly or that shows surprise:<span class="x-gs"><span class="x-g"><span class="rx-g"><span class="x">She gave the officer a blank stare and shrugged her shoulders.</span></span></span></span></span><span class="li"><span class="eb">glimpse</span> a look at somebody/​something for a very short time, when you do not see the person or thing completely:<span class="x-gs"><span class="x-g"><span class="rx-g"><span class="x">He caught a glimpse of her in the crowd.</span></span></span></span></span><span class="li"><span class="eb">glare</span> a long angry look at somebody/​something:<span class="x-gs"><span class="x-g"><span class="rx-g"><span class="x">She fixed her questioner with a hostile glare.</span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="h3">Patterns</span><span class="bullet"><span class="li"> a look/​glance <span class="eb">at</span> somebody/​something</span><span class="li"> a <span class="eb">penetrating/​piercing</span> look/​glance/​gaze/​stare</span><span class="li"> a <span class="eb">long</span> look/​glance/​stare</span><span class="li"> a <span class="eb">brief</span> look/​glance/​glimpse</span><span class="li"> to <span class="eb">have/​get/​take</span> a look/​glance/​glimpse</span><span class="li"> to <span class="eb">avoid</span> somebody’s glance/​gaze/​stare</span></span></span></span></span></li></span> <span class="res-g"><span class="collapse" otitle="Word Origin"><span class="unbox is-active"> <span class="heading" onclick="if(this.parentNode.className=='unbox'){this.parentNode.className='unbox is-active';}else if(this.parentNode.className=='unbox is-active'){this.parentNode.className='unbox';}">Word Origin</span><span class="body"> <span class="def"><span class="lang">late Middle English</span></span> (in the sense <span class="qt">‘rebound obliquely’</span>): probably a nasalized form of obsolete <span class="etym_i">glace</span> in the same sense, from <span class="lang">Old French</span> <span class="ff">glacier</span> ‘to slip’, from <span class="ff">glace</span> ‘ice’, based on <span class="lang">Latin</span> <span class="ff">glacies</span>.</span></span></span><span class="collapse" otitle="Extra examples"><span class="unbox"><span class="heading"
